2002-09-15 Sunday 21:48  pimp-rod

	* WHATSNEW (1.94), src/config/default.xml (1.9),
	src/main/org/openorb/iiop/IIOPClientRequest.java (1.12),
	src/main/org/openorb/iiop/IIOPServerProtocol.java (1.18),

	src/main/org/openorb/iiop/IIOPTransportClientInitializer.java
	(1.10),
	src/main/org/openorb/iiop/IIOPTransportServerInitializer.java
	(1.15), src/main/org/openorb/net/AbstractClientRequest.java (1.11):
	
	- Optimized IIOPClientRequest so that is doesn't have to catch an
	INV_POLICY   each time it is instantiated and the
	SYNC_SCOPE_POLICY_TYPE isn't set.
	
	- Added configuration enhancements to allow greater control on how
	servers   listen for connections, replacing hardcoded values. New
	properties added:	iiop.serverMaxSocketAcceptTimeout      
	iiop.serverMinSocketAcceptTimeout      
	iiop.serverOverrideSocketTimeout
	
	- Added configuration enhancements to allow the a
	BufferedOutputStream to be   used on socket output stream. New
	property added:       iiop.bufferedOutputStreamSize
	
	- Added configuration enhancements to allow the control of
	SO_SNDBUF and	SO_RCVBUF socket properties. New properties added: 
	     iiop.recieveBufferSize	  iiop.sendBufferSize
	
	- Changed default value for iiop.boostReceivePriority as it assumed
	that most   people would be running NT4.0. Default is now false and
	NT4.0 users should   explicitly enable it.

2002-06-28 Friday 12:55  mrumpf

	* src/build.xml (1.72):
	
	    Do not use the version number in the top level directory when
	creating the
	    source archives. The version number in the folder name
	prohibits the
	    source archives to be used in the same way as the CVS modules.
	    The build.sh/bat scripts want the modules names without version
	numbers
	    when collecting jars from other modules.

2002-05-08 Wednesday 12:43  mrumpf

	* src/main/org/openorb/compiler/generator/IdlToJava.java (1.18):
	
	  When no package is specified, classes must be imported
	explicitly.
	  A simple test case with a user-defined exception "BookException"
	  failed because the JavaToIdl created an import statement
	  "import Book" instead of "import BookException".
	  Internally the "BookException" is converted to the IDL name
	  "BookEx" and when writing the Tie/Stub file the "Ex" was simply
	  removed instead of "ception" added.
	  The method for this is located in OpenORB, because JavaToIdl uses
	  the IDL tree structures from the IdlCompiler, see
	     OpenORB/src/main/org/openorb/compiler/generator/IdlToJava

2002-04-06 Saturday 06:03  gmong

	* src/main/org/openorb/CORBA/dynany/DynAnyImpl.java (1.8):
	
	insert_string()'s type verification did not properly handle bounded
	strings; the actual assignment into the any would have destroyed
	the typecode in the any, so if the any contained an aliased string,
	the alias information would have been lost.  The spec says the
	types of inserted items must be equivalent, not equal, so changed
	that in the type verification code.  insert_wstring() still needs
	the same treatment as insert_string().

2002-02-20 Wednesday 07:28  gmong

	* src/main/org/openorb/CORBA/kernel/Configurator.java (1.9):
	
	Modified the handling of initializers so that standard-compliant
	initializer specification works.  This _could_ break existing
	installations which use almost-standard-compliant initializer
	specification, e.g., use a key of
	org.omg.PortableServer.ORBInitializerClass.* with the class name as
	a value, rather than appending the class name to the key.  Also
	changed the name of _initMods to m_initializedModules, and
	_modInits to m_initializers.  The changes have successfully run TNS
	and OTS from the command line and from within a JVM, using both
	configuration-file configuration and -ignoreXML command-line
	configuration.

2002-02-11 Monday 16:55  gmong

	* src/etc/: examples-manifest.mf (1.3), manifest.mf (1.2),
	test-manifest.mf (1.4), tools-manifest.mf (1.4) (utags:
	OpenORB_1_3_0_BETA1, OpenORB_1_3_0_BETA2):

	Implementation headers into the main header.  Removed the Name:
	header as it's only used to identify the particular file a

	header as it is explicitly created by the jar program.	Added a
	final trailing newline (where absent) as the jar spec does not
	specifically say that one will automatically be added by the jar
	program.
